***buste.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:buste.html>buste</a> (37335)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_French" class="extiw" title="w:Middle French">Middle French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="frm"><a href = vnd.unilang:buste.html>buste</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">busto</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">bustum</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:buste.html>buste</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:busten.html>busten</a></b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl">bustes</b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:buste.html>bustetje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>bust (a sculptural portrayal of a person's head and <a href = vnd.unilang:shoulders.html>shoulders</a>)</li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">breast</span>, of a woman</li></ol>

***buster.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a> (10242)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Originally a dialectal variant of <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">burster</i>; <a href = vnd.unilang:later.html>later</a> influenced by <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">bust</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:dictatoriaal.html>-er</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-oed1_1-0" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-oed1-1"> | 1 | </a></sup>
</p><p>The combining form of the term <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> appeared from the early 20th century but <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> especially prolific during three periods: in the 1930s, owing to the success of the radio series <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gang_Busters" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Gang Busters"><a href = vnd.unilang:gang.html>Gang</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:busters.html>Busters</a></a></i>; in the 1940s, owing to its appearance as military <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a>; and in the 1980s, owing to the success of the movie <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghostbusters" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Ghostbusters"><a href = vnd.unilang:ghostbusters.html>Ghostbusters</a></a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-oed2_2-0" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-oed2-2"> | 2 | </a></sup>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:busters.html>busters</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">chiefly colloquial<span class="ib-comma">,</span> with 'of'</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Someone who or something that bursts, <a href = vnd.unilang:breaks.html>breaks</a>, or destroys a specified thing.
<ul><li><b>1614</b>, S. Jerome, <i>Moses his Sight of Canaan</i>, 147:
<dl><dd>Now death, I pray <a href = vnd.unilang:thee.html>thee</a> what <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> it, but a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b> of <a href = vnd.unilang:bonds.html>bonds</a>; a destruction of toyle?</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2005</b>, J. Madhavan, <i>Sita amp; Forest <a href = vnd.unilang:bandits.html>Bandits</a></i>, 122:
<dl><dd>Rothlin <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> described... by the papers as the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b> of the <a href = vnd.unilang:bandit.html>bandit</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:ring.html>ring</a>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">chiefly military  <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Forming compounds denoting a team, weapon, or device specialized in the destruction of the first element</span>.
<ul><li><b>1940</b> September 2, <i>Life</i>, 29/1:
<dl><dd>German ‘<b>balloon <a href = vnd.unilang:busters.html>busters</a></b>’ attack the Dover barrage.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1958</b> February 10, <i>Life</i>, 70:
<dl><dd>Our main purpose in further experimentation with nuclear bombs <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> not... to make <b>city-busters</b> more horrible.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">chiefly colloquial<span class="ib-comma">,</span> with 'of'</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Someone who or something that '<a href = vnd.unilang:breaks.html>breaks</a>', tames, or overpowers a specified person or thing.
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> in particular<span class="ib-comma">,</span> dated<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A broncobuster.
<ul><li><b>1891</b> July, <i>Harper's Magazine</i>, 208/2
<dl><dd>The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b> must be careful to keep well away from sheds and timber.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1964</b>,  John Hendrix,  <cite>If I Can Do It Horseback: A Cow-Country Sketchbook</cite>, page 40:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Some <b><a href = vnd.unilang:busters.html>busters</a></b> caught their <a href = vnd.unilang:horses.html>horses</a> for the first time <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> the head, and snubbed or choked them until they fell gasping.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">chiefly law enforcement  <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Forming compounds denoting an <a href = vnd.unilang:agent.html>agent</a> or agency tasked with reducing or eliminating the first element</span>.
<ul><li><b>1920</b>, F. A. McKenzie, <i>‘Pussyfoot’ Johnson</i>, v. 83:
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:men.html>Men</a> nicknamed him the ‘<b>Booze <a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>Buster</a></b>’, and cartoonists <a href = vnd.unilang:loved.html>loved</a> to picture him, <a href = vnd.unilang:revolver.html>revolver</a> in hand,... fighting the <a href = vnd.unilang:demon.html>demon</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:rum.html>rum</a>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><i>1974'</i> July 4, <i>New Scientist</i>, 65/2:
<dl><dd>The professional <b>fraud-busters</b> [of the art world].</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1984</b> November 18, <i>N.Y. Times</i>, iv. 24/2:
<dl><dd>New York City traffic agents have become <b>Gridlock <a href = vnd.unilang:busters.html>Busters</a></b> and cigarette foes are <b>smokebusters</b>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">dated<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Someone or something remarkable, especially for being loud, large, etc..
<ul><li><b>1833</b> April, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:parthenon.html>Parthenon</a></i>, 293:
<dl><dd>‘I <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> to clean this old roarer,’ continued the ‘editor’... as he wiped the barrel of his pistol. ‘She's a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b>, I tell you.’</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2004</b> November 20, <i>South Wales Echo</i>, 9:
<dl><dd>What a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b> of a <a href = vnd.unilang:lunch.html>lunch</a> it <a href = vnd.unilang:turned.html>turned</a> out to be.</dd></dl></li></ul>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">colloquial<span class="ib-comma">,</span> variously expressing familiarity, admiration, or hostility</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">A form of address, particularly of <a href = vnd.unilang:men.html>men</a></span>: guy, dude, fella, <a href = vnd.unilang:mack.html>mack</a>, <a href = vnd.unilang:buddy.html>buddy</a>, <a href = vnd.unilang:loser.html>loser</a>. (<i>Originally as 'old <a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a>'</i>.)
<ul><li><b>1838</b> March 24, <i>New Yorker</i>, 4/1:
<dl><dd>That's generous, <b>old <a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1919</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P.G._Wodehouse" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:P.G. Wodehouse">P.G. Wodehouse</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/My_Man_Jeeves" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:My Man Jeeves">My <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>Man</a> Jeeves</a></i>, 79:
<dl><dd>An extremely wealthy <b>old <a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2001</b>, S. MacKay, <i>Fall Guy</i>, ix. 113:
<dl><dd>‘Careful, <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b>,’ she <a href = vnd.unilang:said.html>said</a>. ‘I've got a knife in my hand.’</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A loaf of bread.
<ul><li><b>1835</b> September 16, <i>Morning Post</i>, 4/2:
<dl><dd>Three <a href = vnd.unilang:penny.html>penny</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:busters.html>busters</a></b>, and a whole kit-full of winegar and mustard.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1904</b> June 8, <i>Journal of the Department of Labour</i> (New Zealand), 536:
<dl><dd>An 8oz. loaf of brown bread... goes by the name of ‘<b><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b>’, I suppose on account of the way they blow you out.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A drinking spree, a binge.
<ul><li><b>1848</b>, John Russell Bartlett, <i>Dictionary of Americanisms</i>:
<dl><dd>They <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> on a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a></b>, and <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:taken.html>taken</a> up by the police.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1922</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Joyce" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:James Joyce">James Joyce</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulysses_(novel)" class="extiw" title="w:Ulysses (novel)">Ulysses</a></i>, 405:

<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">dated<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A gale, a strong wind; <span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">especially <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia" class="extiw" title="w:Australia">Australia</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> a southerly <a href = vnd.unilang:buster.html>buster</a>.

***butch.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a> (13126)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Originally, it <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> probably used as an abbreviation of <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">butcher</i>. <a href = vnd.unilang:later.html>Later</a>, in the 1940s, the sense "masculine lesbian" <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> developed.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjective">Adjective</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></strong> (<i>comparative</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en comparative-form-of" lang="en">butcher</b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en comparative-form-of" lang="en">more <a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b>, <i>superlative</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en superlative-form-of" lang="en">butchest</b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en superlative-form-of" lang="en">most <a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> originally  Polari</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Very masculine, with a masculine appearance or attitude.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1967</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenneth_Williams" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Kenneth Williams">Kenneth Williams</a> as <a href = vnd.unilang:sandy.html>Sandy</a>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Round_the_Horne" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Round the Horne">Round the <a href = vnd.unilang:horne.html>Horne</a></a></cite>, written by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barry_Took" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Barry Took"><a href = vnd.unilang:barry.html>Barry</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:took.html>Took</a></a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marty_Feldmen" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Marty Feldmen">Marty Feldmen</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">There, look, <a href = vnd.unilang:mr.html>Mr</a>. <a href = vnd.unilang:horne.html>Horne</a>! Vada that great <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b> lucoddy!</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1979</b>, Colin MacInnes, <i>Out of the way: <a href = vnd.unilang:later.html>later</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:essays.html>essays</a></i>:
<dl><dd>Nor can I credit that a — to put it crudely — proud bisexual <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b> Italian — albeit  one lonely, poor, emotional and without strong will — which Giovanni <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> shown to  be in the earlier part of the book, should become, in a mere matter of months, and as the result of any happening, the venal hysterical fairy that he does.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1998</b>,  Weston, <a href = vnd.unilang:kath.html>Kath</a>,  <cite>Render <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>Me</a>, Gender <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>Me</a>: Lesbians Talk Sex, Class, Color, Nation, Studmuffins</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=UZ-IHCxcqHACamp;pg=PT7amp;dq=%22more+butch%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ved=0ahUKEwiJ_InU79rOAhVU8mMKHTxUA_sQ6AEIHDAAv=onepageamp;q=%22more%20butch%22amp;f=false">[1]</a></sup>, Columbia University Press, <small>→ISBN</small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Then I started going out with different <a href = vnd.unilang:kinds.html>kinds</a> of women, and I started feeling more like <i>I</i> <a href = vnd.unilang:wanted.html>wanted</a> to be more <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b>. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> I feel much more <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b> than I feel <a href = vnd.unilang:femme.html>femme</a>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>2007</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:beth.html>Beth</a> A. Firestein, <i>Becoming Visible: Counseling Bisexuals Across the Lifespan</i>, Columbia University Press (→ISBN), page 305:
<dl><dd>The process of appreciating a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b> aesthetic may be <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>even</a> more complex for bisexual <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b> women. In contrast to lesbian butches who may date only within a butch-femme community, bisexual <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b> women may be more likely to <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> In comparison to <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b> bisexual women, it may be easier for <a href = vnd.unilang:femme.html>femme</a> bisexual women to locate male and female <a href = vnd.unilang:dating.html>dating</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:partners.html>partners</a> <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2014</b>, Naomi S <a href = vnd.unilang:tucker.html>Tucker</a>, <i>Bisexual Politics: <a href = vnd.unilang:theories.html>Theories</a>, Queries, and Visions</i>, Routledge (→ISBN), page 186:
<dl><dd>More of the <a href = vnd.unilang:rotten.html>rotten</a> responses I receive about being a bisexual <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b> woman come from other bisexuals, particularly <a href = vnd.unilang:men.html>men</a>, who don'<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> want to deal with any woman who <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> not some <a href = vnd.unilang:barbie.html>Barbie</a> doll standard of femininity.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:macho.html>macho</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">manly</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">mannish</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">unfeminine</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">masc</span></li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<div class="sister-wikipedia sister-project noprint floatright" style="border: 1px solid aaa; font-size: 90%; background: f9f9f9; width: 250px; padding: 4px; text-align: left;"><div style="float: left;"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/44px-Wikipedia-logo.png" decoding="async" width="44" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/66px-Wikipedia-logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/88px-Wikipedia-logo.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200" /></div></div><div style="margin-left: 60px;">English Wikipedia <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> an article on:<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butch_and_femme" class="extiw" title="w:Butch and femme"><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>Butch</a> and <a href = vnd.unilang:femme.html>femme</a></a></b></div></div><span class="interProject"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butch_and_femme" class="extiw" title="w:Butch and femme">Wikipedia </a></span></div>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">butches</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> LGBT<span class="ib-comma">,</span> countable</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A lesbian who appears masculine or <a href = vnd.unilang:acts.html>acts</a> in a masculine manner.
<ul><li><b>1997</b>, Bi Academic Intervention, <i>Bisexual Imaginary: Representation, Identity, and Desire</i>, Aamp;C Black (→ISBN), page 30, quoting <a href = vnd.unilang:jo.html>Jo</a> Eadie:
<dl><dd>Coming out appeals to the narcissistic pleasure of presenting to another a finished image of ourselves, which they return to us in exactly the same form: [someone <a href = vnd.unilang:tells.html>tells</a>] you [they are] a bisexual <b><a href = vnd.unilang:butch.html>butch</a></b>, and you confirm it. But instead, it seems all too likely – especially, perhaps, for bisexuals, whose claims to identity always need that much more proof – that no such mirror-image will be returned.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>

***butcher.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> butcher (8710)</h1><br><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zelfstandig_naamwoord"><i><a href = vnd.unilang:zelfstandig.html>Zelfstandig</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:naamwoord.html>naamwoord</a></i></span></h4>

***buttercup.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:buttercup.html>buttercup</a> (45739)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">butter</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">cup</i>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:buttercup.html>buttercup</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">buttercups</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Any of many herbs, of the genus <i>Ranunculus</i>, having yellow flowers; the crowfoot.</li>
<li>Any flower of the genus <i><a href = vnd.unilang:narcissus.html>Narcissus</a></i>; a daffodil.</li>
<li><span class="use-with-mention">Affectionate or ironic term of address.</span>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1987</b>,  Joyce <a href = vnd.unilang:brandon.html>Brandon</a>,  <cite>Lady and the Lawman</cite>, page 346:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Listen, <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buttercup.html>buttercup</a></b>, you're damned good in <a href = vnd.unilang:bed.html>bed</a>. They don'<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> come any better, but I'm really not interested in playing second fiddle to your <a href = vnd.unilang:camera.html>camera</a> or your young <a href = vnd.unilang:lovers.html>lovers</a>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">ranunculus</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">crowfoot</span></li></ul>

***buurt.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:buurt.html>buurt</a> (523)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:buurt.html>buurt</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">district</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> (also <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">buyrte</i>) [15th century], from <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">ghebuerte</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">surroundings</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> [c. 1290] and <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">gebuerde</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">zone</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> [c. 1240], related to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">giburida</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-1"> | 1 | </a></sup>  Akin to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:West Frisian language">West Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fy">buert</i>. See also
<i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:gebied.html>gebied</a></i> and Belgian Dutch synonym <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">gebuurte</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:buurt.html>buurt</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:buurten.html>buurten</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:buurtje.html>buurtje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>neighborhood, part of town.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl">Tivoli <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:een.html>een</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buurt.html>buurt</a></b> in Eindhoven.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">Tivoli <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a <b>neighbourhood</b> in Eindhoven.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>vicinity, proximity
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>Hij</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <b>in <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:buurt.html>buurt</a></b>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">He <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <b>close by</b>.</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl">Groningen <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:nogal.html>nogal</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:uit.html>uit</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:buurt.html>buurt</a></b>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">Groningen <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> rather <b>out of the way</b>.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>

***buzzard.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:buzzard.html>buzzard</a> (94768)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Norman_language" class="extiw" title="w:Anglo-Norman language">Anglo-Norman</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">buisart</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">buison</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">buson</i> (<span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">buse</i>), possibly from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">buteō</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:buzzard.html>buzzard</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:buzzards.html>buzzards</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Any of several Old World <a href = vnd.unilang:birds.html>birds</a> of prey of the genus <i>Buteo</i> with broad wings and a broad tail.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">Canada, US</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Any scavenging bird such as the American black vulture (<i>Coragyps atratus</i>) or the turkey vulture (<i>Cathartes aura</i>).</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">colloquial<span class="ib-comma">,</span> derogatory<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> often preceded by "old", the "old <a href = vnd.unilang:buzzard.html>buzzard</a>"</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> In North America, a curmudgeonly or cantankerous <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a>; an old person; a mean, greedy person.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1995</b>,  LaRee Bryant,  <cite>Forever, My Love</cite>, page 88:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Perhaps the crusty old <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buzzard.html>buzzard</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:loved.html>loved</a> his only child more than anyone <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> given him credit for all these years — maybe <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>even</a> more than he himself <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> realized.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">archaic</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A blockhead; a dunce.
<ul><li><b>1640</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Herbert" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:George Herbert">George Herbert</a>, <i>Jacula Prudentum; or, Outlandish Proverbs, Sentences, etc.</i>, in <i>The <a href = vnd.unilang:remains.html>Remains</a> of that Sweet Singer of the Temple George Herbert</i>, London: Pickering, 1841, p. 142,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://archive.org/details/remainsofthats00her">[1]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>An old <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a>’s shadow <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> better than a young <b><a href = vnd.unilang:buzzard.html>buzzard</a></b>’s sword.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1774</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oliver_Goldsmith" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Oliver Goldsmith"><a href = vnd.unilang:oliver.html>Oliver</a> Goldsmith</a>, <i>Animated Nature</i>, Volume 6, Index,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.ca/books?id=GK5EAAAAYAAJamp;printsec=frontcoverv=onepageamp;qamp;f=false">[2]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>It <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> common, to a proverb, to call one who can not be taught, or who continues obstinately ignorant, <b>a <a href = vnd.unilang:buzzard.html>buzzard</a></b>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">golf</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Synonym of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">double <a href = vnd.unilang:bogey.html>bogey</a></i></span></span></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">buteo</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">broadwing</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">turkey vulture</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">vulture</span></li></ul>
</body>

<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:bye-bye.html>bye-bye</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">informal<span class="ib-comma">,</span> often childish</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Goodbye.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:bye-bye.html>bye-bye</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">bye-byes</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">colloquial<span class="ib-comma">,</span> often childish</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A goodbye.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">colloquial<span class="ib-comma">,</span> often childish</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Bedtime for a toddler, going to sleep, going to <a href = vnd.unilang:bed.html>bed</a>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Brush your teeth, it's time to go <a href = vnd.unilang:bye-bye.html>bye-bye</a>.</i></div></dd>

***cabinepersoneel.html

***cafetaria.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cafetaria.html>cafetaria</a> (13493)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">cafeteria</i>, from American <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Spanish language">Spanish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="es">cafetería</i>. The shift to <i>cafet<b>a</b><a href = vnd.unilang:ria.html>ria</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> because of influence of other nouns on <i>-taria</i> and <i>-aria</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Snackbar.jpg/200px-Snackbar.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Snackbar.jpg/300px-Snackbar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Snackbar.jpg/400px-Snackbar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" />  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"></div><i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:cafetaria.html>Cafetaria</a></b> in Amsterdam</i><br /><b>Snack <a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a></b> in Amsterdam</div></div></div> 
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Eindhoven_-_Cafetaria_Van_Abbemuseum.jpg/200px-Eindhoven_-_Cafetaria_Van_Abbemuseum.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Eindhoven_-_Cafetaria_Van_Abbemuseum.jpg/300px-Eindhoven_-_Cafetaria_Van_Abbemuseum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Eindhoven_-_Cafetaria_Van_Abbemuseum.jpg/400px-Eindhoven_-_Cafetaria_Van_Abbemuseum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" />  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"></div><i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:cafetaria.html>Cafetaria</a></b> in <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:van.html>Van</a> Abbemuseum in Eindhoven</i><br /><b>Dining area</b> in the <a href = vnd.unilang:van.html>Van</a> Abbe museum in Eindhoven</div></div></div>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:cafetaria.html>cafetaria</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:cafetaria.html>cafetaria</a>'s</b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:cafetaria.html>cafetariaatje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>small <a href = vnd.unilang:restaurant.html>restaurant</a>, cafeteria</li>
<li>snack <a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a></li></ol>

***calabash.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> (108374)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Crescentia_cujete_WS.JPG/200px-Crescentia_cujete_WS.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Crescentia_cujete_WS.JPG/300px-Crescentia_cujete_WS.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Crescentia_cujete_WS.JPG/400px-Crescentia_cujete_WS.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1360" /></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> or <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> tree (<i>Crescentia cujete</i>; <i>sense 1</i>) and its fruit</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/B%E1%BA%A7u_n%E1%BA%ADm.jpg/200px-B%E1%BA%A7u_n%E1%BA%ADm.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/B%E1%BA%A7u_n%E1%BA%ADm.jpg/300px-B%E1%BA%A7u_n%E1%BA%ADm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/B%E1%BA%A7u_n%E1%BA%ADm.jpg/400px-B%E1%BA%A7u_n%E1%BA%ADm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a>, <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> vine, or bottle gourd (<i>Lagenaria siceraria</i>; <i>sense 2</i>) and its fruit</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Jalpa_de_M%C3%A9ndez_Artesan%C3%ADas.jpg/200px-Jalpa_de_M%C3%A9ndez_Artesan%C3%ADas.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Jalpa_de_M%C3%A9ndez_Artesan%C3%ADas.jpg/300px-Jalpa_de_M%C3%A9ndez_Artesan%C3%ADas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Jalpa_de_M%C3%A9ndez_Artesan%C3%ADas.jpg/400px-Jalpa_de_M%C3%A9ndez_Artesan%C3%ADas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Calabashes <i>(sense 3)</i>, <a href = vnd.unilang:containers.html>containers</a> made from fruits of the <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> tree, from <a href = vnd.unilang:tabasco.html>Tabasco</a>, Mexico</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hula_calabash.jpg/200px-Hula_calabash.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hula_calabash.jpg/300px-Hula_calabash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hula_calabash.jpg/400px-Hula_calabash.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">An ipu, a Hawaiian <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> <i>(sense 5)</i> often used to provide a beat for <a href = vnd.unilang:hula.html>hula</a> dancing. It <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> made from two fruit of the <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> vine joined together</div></div></div></div>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">calebasse</i>, from <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> or directly from its etymon <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Persian language">Persian</a></span> <i class="fa-Arab mention" lang="fa">خربزه</i> |  <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="fa-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">xarboze</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">melon</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-OED_1-0" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-OED-1"> | 1 | </a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-2"> | 2 | </a></sup> possibly ultimately from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit" class="extiw" title="w:Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a></span> <i class="Deva mention" lang="sa">त्रपुस</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="sa-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">trapusa</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">colocynth fruit</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> (compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Persian language">Persian</a></span> <i class="fa-Arab mention" lang="fa">تربزه</i> |  <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="fa-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">tarboze</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">watermelon</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>). The English word <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalan_language" class="extiw" title="w:Catalan language">Catalan</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ca">carabassa</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">pumpkin; orange colour</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galician_language" class="extiw" title="w:Galician language">Galician</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gl">cabaza</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">gourd, pumpkin, squash; <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> (container)</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occitan_language" class="extiw" title="w:Occitan language">Occitan</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="oc">calebasso</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="oc">carabasso</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="oc">carbasso</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portuguese_language" class="extiw" title="w:Portuguese language">Portuguese</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="pt">cabaça</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">gourd; <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> (container)</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sicilian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Sicilian language">Sicilian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="scn">caravazza</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-OED_1-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-OED-1"> | 1 | </a></sup>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">calabashes</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A tree (known as the <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> tree; <i>Crescentia cujete</i>) native to Central and South America, the West Indies, and southern Florida, bearing large, round fruit used to make <a href = vnd.unilang:containers.html>containers</a> <i>(sense 3)</i>; the fruit of this tree.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1821</b>,  Alexander <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> Humboldt [<i>i.e.</i>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a>] |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aim%C3%A9_Bonpland" class="extiw" title="w:Aimé Bonpland">Aimé Bonpland</a>,  chapter XXI, in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helen_Maria_Williams" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Helen Maria Williams"><a href = vnd.unilang:helen.html>Helen</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:maria.html>Maria</a> Williams</a>, transl., <cite>Personal Narrative of Travels to the Equinoctial Regions of the New Continent, during the Years 1799–1804. <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span> Written in French<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="by Alexander de Humboldt">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, and <a href = vnd.unilang:translated.html>Translated</a> into English<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="by Helen Maria Williams.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite>, volume V, London |  Printed for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Longman" class="extiw" title="w:Longman">Longman, <a href = vnd.unilang:hurst.html>Hurst</a>, <a href = vnd.unilang:rees.html>Rees</a>, Orme, and Brown</a>,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="Paternoster Row.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/861227170">861227170</a></small>, book VII, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=vD0UAAAAYAAJamp;pg=PA129">page 129</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">As <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> absolutely destitute of large vessels, to contain and mix liquids, <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> poured, by means of a <i>tutuma</i> (fruit of <i>crescentia cujete</i>, <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a></b>), the water of the river into one of the <a href = vnd.unilang:holes.html>holes</a> of the rock. To this <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> added sugar, and the juice of acid fruits. In a few minutes <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> an excellent beverage, which <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> almost a refinement of luxury in that wild spot; [...]</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1870</b>,  “Goso, the Teacher”, in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Steere" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Edward Steere">Edward Steere</a>, transl., <cite><a href = vnd.unilang:swahili.html>Swahili</a> Tales, as <a href = vnd.unilang:told.html>Told</a> by Natives of <a href = vnd.unilang:zanzibar.html>Zanzibar</a>. With an English Translation</cite>, London |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Bell_%26_Sons" class="extiw" title="w:George Bell amp; Sons">Bell amp; Daldy</a>,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="York Street, Covent Garden.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/250333102">250333102</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=KCBKAAAAcAAJamp;pg=PA287">page 287</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">There <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> a teacher who taught children to read under a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a></b> tree, and this teacher's name <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> Goso.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>The bottle gourd (<a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a> vine, <i>Lagenaria siceraria</i>), believed to have originated in Africa, which <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> grown for its fruit that are used as a vegetable and to make <a href = vnd.unilang:containers.html>containers</a> <i>(sense 3)</i>; the fruit of this plant.
<dl><dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonyms:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">dudhi</span> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">India</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">lauki</span> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">India</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span></span></dd></dl>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1839</b> January,  “L.”,  “The <a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>Calabash</a> (<i>Cucurbita Lagenaria</i>)”, in  <cite>The Visitor, or Monthly Instructor</cite>, London |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_Tract_Society" class="extiw" title="w:Religious Tract Society">The Religious Tract Society</a>; [...] <a href = vnd.unilang:sold.html>sold</a> by John Davis,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="at the Depository, 56, Paternoster Row, and 65, St. Paul’s Churchyard,; and by the booksellers.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/740304389">740304389</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=AAcbAAAAYAAJamp;pg=PA75">page 75</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a></b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a <a href = vnd.unilang:kind.html>kind</a> of gourd, and <a href = vnd.unilang:belongs.html>belongs</a> to that family of twining plants which <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> called among the Hebrews, "wild <a href = vnd.unilang:vines.html>vines</a>," but by the botanists of modern times, the <i>cucurbitaceæ</i>, or cucurbitaceous plants. [...] That playful variety of form and magnitude, so remarkable in the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a></b>, renders it fit for all <a href = vnd.unilang:kinds.html>kinds</a> of uses. Sometimes <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> have a globular base, terminating in a long neck, and then it answers the purpose of a bottle, and the American fastens it to his girdle, or the pommel of his saddle, when about to pass through regions which abound not in water.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2008</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_A._Duke" class="extiw" title="w:James A. Duke">James A. <li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2009</b>,  <a href = vnd.unilang:charlie.html>Charlie</a> Nardozzi and <a href = vnd.unilang:editors.html>editors</a> of the National Gardening Association,  “Sweet Corn and an A to <a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a> of Other Worthy Veggies”, in  <cite>Vegetable Gardening for <a href = vnd.unilang:dummies.html>Dummies</a></cite> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/For_Dummies" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:For Dummies">For <a href = vnd.unilang:dummies.html>Dummies</a></a> series), 2nd edition, Hoboken, N.J. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiley_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Wiley (publisher)">Wiley Publishing</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, part II (Vegging Out), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=1ANqvBDcKNICamp;pg=PA167">page 167</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Asian gourds grow like cucumbers [...] and feature strong flavors that are often used in Indian, Chinese, and Southeast Asian <a href = vnd.unilang:soups.html>soups</a> and stews. Some <a href = vnd.unilang:types.html>types</a> to try in your garden include the bitter gourd and <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a></b> gourd.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>A container made from the mature, dried shell of the fruit of one of the above plants; also, a similarly shaped container made from some other material.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1799</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mungo_Park_(explorer)" class="extiw" title="w:Mungo Park (explorer)"><a href = vnd.unilang:mungo.html>Mungo</a> Park</a>,  “Of Gold-dust, and the Manner in which It <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> Collected.—Process of Washing it.—<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Its Value in Africa.—Of Ivory.—Surprise of the Negroes at the Eagerness of the Europeans for This Commodity.—Scattered Teeth Frequently Picked up in the Woods.—Mode of Hunting the Elephant.—Some Reflections on the Unimproved State of the Country, amp;c.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>”, in  <cite>Travels in the Interior <a href = vnd.unilang:districts.html>Districts</a> of Africa: Performed under the Direction and Patronage of the African Association, in the Years 1795, 1796, and 1797.<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title=" | ... |  With an Appendix, Containing Geographical Illustrations of Africa: By Major Rennell.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite>, London |  Printed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Bulmer_(printer)" class="extiw" title="w:William Bulmer (printer)">W[illiam] Bulmer and Co.</a> for the author; for when the searchers return from the valleys in the evening, they commonly bring with them each a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a></b> or two of sand, to be washed by such of the females as remain at home.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1851</b> November 14,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herman_Melville" class="extiw" title="w:Herman Melville">Herman Melville</a>,  “Wheelbarrow” and “The Prophet”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moby-Dick" class="extiw" title="w:Moby-Dick">Moby-Dick; or, The Whale</a></cite>, 1st American edition, New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harper_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Harper (publisher)">Harper amp; Brothers</a>; London: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Bentley_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Richard Bentley (publisher)">Richard Bentley</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/57395299">57395299</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/mobydickorwhale01melvpage/65/mode/1up">pages 65 and 105</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"> | <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/mobydickorwhale01melvpage/65/mode/1up">page 65</a> |  The people of his island of Rokovoko, it seems, at their wedding feasts express the fragrant water of young cocoanuts into a large stained <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calabash.html>calabash</a></b> like a punchbowl; and this punchbowl always forms the great central ornament on the braided mat where the feast <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:held.html>held</a>. it conſiſts of ſixteen <b>calabaſhes</b> orderly placed along the middle between two ſide-boards joined together, or a long frame, hanging about a <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a>'s neck with a <a href = vnd.unilang:thong.html>thong</a>. <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>Over</a> the mouths of the <b>calabaſhes</b> there are thin ſounding ſlips of red wood called Tanilla, a little above a ſpan long, which being beaten with two little ſticks, <a href = vnd.unilang:returns.html>returns</a> a ſound from the <b>calabaſhes</b> of ſeveral ſizes not unlike an organ.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>

***calamiteit.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:calamiteit.html>calamiteit</a> (108373)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">calamité</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_French" class="extiw" title="w:Middle French">Middle French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="frm">calamité</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">calamitās</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:calamiteit.html>calamiteit</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:calamiteiten.html>calamiteiten</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:calamiteit.html>calamiteitje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>large <span class="Latn" lang="en">disaster</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">calamity</span> <span class="defdate">[from 17th c.]</span></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ramp.html>ramp</a></span></li></ul>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zelfstandig_naamwoord"><i><a href = vnd.unilang:zelfstandig.html>Zelfstandig</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:naamwoord.html>naamwoord</a></i></span></h4>
<p><b><a href = vnd.unilang:calamiteit.html>calamiteit</a></b> <span style="background-color: f8f9fa;border-radius: 2px;border: 1px solid c8ccd1;padding: 0 0.2em 0 0.1em;font-style: italic">v</span>

***caleidoscoop.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:caleidoscoop.html>caleidoscoop</a> (61497)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">kaleidoscope</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">καλός</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">kalós</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">beautiful</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">εἶδος</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">eîdos</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">shape</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> (compare <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">-oid</i>)  + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">-scope</i>. Coined 1817, by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Brewster" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:David Brewster">David <a href = vnd.unilang:brewster.html>Brewster</a></a>, its inventor.<sup id="cite_ref-oetyld_1-0" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-oetyld-1"> | 1 | </a></sup>
</p><p>Figurative sense of “constantly changing pattern” attested 1819 by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lord_Byron" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a>, who <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> received a kaleidoscope from his publisher.<sup id="cite_ref-oetyld_1-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-oetyld-1"> | 1 | </a></sup>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>

</p>
<ol><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">kaleidoscope</span></li></ol>

***calico.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:calico.html>calico</a> (65697)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From Calicut, in India, from where the cloth <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> originally exported, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malayalam" class="extiw" title="w:Malayalam">Malayalam</a></span> <i class="Mlym mention" lang="ml">കോഴിക്കോട്</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ml-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">kōḻikkōṭŭ</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">Kozhikode</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <i class="Mlym mention" lang="ml">കോഴി</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ml-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">kōḻi</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">palace</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + <i class="Mlym mention" lang="ml">ക്കോട്</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ml-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">kkōṭŭ</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">fortified palace</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, with ‘y’ replaced by interchangeable ‘zh’.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:calico.html>calico</a></strong> (<i>countable and uncountable</i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">calicos</b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">calicoes</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">textiles</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <a href = vnd.unilang:kind.html>kind</a> of rough cloth made from unbleached and not fully processed cotton, often printed with a bright pattern.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1832</b>,  Michael Faraday,  “Experimental Researches in Electricity”, in  <cite>Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society of London</cite>, volume 122, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" class="extiw" title="w:Digital object identifier">DOI</a>:<span class="neverexpand"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1098%2Frstl.1832.0006">10.1098/rstl.1832.0006</a></span></small>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JSTOR" class="extiw" title="w:JSTOR">JSTOR</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/stable/107956">107956</a></small>, page 126:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">This helix <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> covered with <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calico.html>calico</a></b>, and then a second wire applied in the same manner.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">countable<span class="ib-comma">,</span> zoology</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Ellipsis of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:calico.html>calico</a> cat</i></span></span>; a cat with fur of the colors black, white and orange.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjective">Adjective</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:calico.html>calico</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>Having a pattern of red and contrasting areas, resembling the color of <a href = vnd.unilang:calico.html>calico</a> cloth.
<dl><dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonym:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">tortoiseshell</span></span></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calico.html>calico</a></b> cat <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> distinctive red and dark markings.</i></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:calico.html>calico</a></b>-patterned tablecloths <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> supposed to make the <a href = vnd.unilang:restaurant.html>restaurant</a> look rustic; instead, they made it look run down.</i></div></dd></dl></li></ol>
</body>
